GT (fixed):  
\[
f(\epsilon,T)= -0.6056800229\,(T-298.0016449)\;+\;\epsilon\cdot 3.1473717381\cdot \exp\!\big(-(T-298.0016449)^2\big)
\]
So GT is **affine in \(T\)** plus an **\(\epsilon\)-linear term whose coefficient is a Gaussian in \(T\)**. In particular:
- Dependence on \(\epsilon\) is exactly linear (no \(\epsilon^2\), \(\exp(\epsilon)\), \(\log(\epsilon)\), etc.).
- The \(\epsilon\)-coefficient is \(\;3.1473\exp(-(T-298.0016)^2)\), which is **not** constant, not exponential-in-\(T\), not rational-in-\(T\), not log-in-\(T\), etc.
- The \(T\)-only part is exactly linear: \(-0.60568\,T + \text{constant}\).

Now check candidates: to match GT, each candidate must be reducible (by setting its constants) to “linear in \(T\) + \(\epsilon\cdot(\text{Gaussian in }T)\)”.

---

### 1
Has terms like \(T c0 \epsilon\) (gives \(\epsilon T\) cross-term), \(c1\exp(c2\epsilon)\) (nonlinear in \(\epsilon\)), \(\epsilon\log(Tc5+1)\), and \(\exp(c7/(T+c8))\exp(c9\epsilon)\). Cannot reduce to \(\epsilon\cdot \exp(-(T-a)^2)\) while also keeping a separate linear-in-\(T\) term. **No.**

### 2

### 3

### 4
Includes \(\exp(c7\epsilon)/T^5\): nonlinear in \(\epsilon\) and wrong \(T\) form. **No.**

### 5

GT: -c0*(T - c1) + epsilon*c2*exp(-(T - c3)**c4)

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT:** `-0.6057*(T - 298.00) + epsilon*3.1474*exp(-(T - 298.00)²)`

Expanding: `-0.6057*T + 0.6057*298.00 + epsilon*3.1474*exp(-(T-298)²)`

This simplifies to: `c_a*T + c_b + epsilon*c_c*exp(-(T-298)²)`

The key structural elements are:
1. A linear term in T (no epsilon dependence)
2. A constant term (no epsilon or T dependence)
3. A term that is linear in epsilon multiplied by a Gaussian in T: `epsilon * exp(-T²)` type term

Let me check each candidate for structural compatibility with these basis functions.

The critical term is `epsilon*exp(-(T-c)²)` — a Gaussian in T multiplied by epsilon. Most candidates don't have this structure.

Let me scan for candidates that could produce `epsilon*exp(-(T-c)²)`:

**Candidates 1-8, 41:** These have forms like `T*c0*epsilon + ... + epsilon*log(T*c5+1)`. The `T*epsilon` and `epsilon*log(T+c)` terms cannot combine to form a pure linear T term plus a Gaussian. These have epsilon-dependent terms that can't be zeroed without losing the Gaussian. None of these contain `exp(-T²)` type terms.

**Candidates 10, 21, 27, 31, 33, 50:** These contain `exp(T*c)` or `exp(c/T)` terms — exponential in T, not Gaussian.

**Candidate 11:** `T*c0 + c1 + c2*epsilon + c3*epsilon*exp(T*c4) + c5*exp(c6/T)` — has `epsilon*exp(c4*T)` which is exponential, not Gaussian.

**Candidate 34:** `T*c0 + c1*epsilon² + c2*epsilon + c3 + c4*exp(c5/(T+c6))` — has epsilon² (not epsilon*Gaussian(T)), and exp(c/(T+c)) is not Gaussian.

**Candidates 18, 29, 37, 46-49:** These are polynomial in epsilon and T — no Gaussian possible.

**Candidates 24, 25, 45, 20, 13, 12:** These have `exp(c*epsilon)` terms but no Gaussian in T multiplied by epsilon.

Going through ALL candidates systematically: The GT requires a term `epsilon * exp(-(T-c)²)` which is a **Gaussian function of T** multiplied by epsilon. None of the candidates contain `exp(-T²)` or `exp(-(T-c)²)` type structures. The exponentials in the candidates are either `exp(c*epsilon)`, `exp(c*T)`, `exp(c/T)`, or `exp(c/(T+d))` — none of which can produce a Gaussian in T.

A Gaussian `exp(-T²)` cannot be represented by `exp(aT)`, `exp(a/T)`, polynomials, logarithms, or any combination thereof. These are fundamentally different basis functions.

Therefore, **no candidate matches**.
